  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3074be22-f392-48d7-a005-3aff09256480'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

    };

<span id="freeTextContainer12496692846919350780">Em is locked in a bare, cold cell with no comforts. Finn is in the cell next door. The Doctor is keeping them there until they tell him what he wants to know. Trouble is, what he wants to know hasn't happened yet. <br/><br/>Em and Finn have a shared past, but no future unless they can find a way out.   <span id="freeText12496692846919350780" style="display:none">Em is locked in a bare, cold cell with no comforts. Finn is in the cell next door. The Doctor is keeping them there until they tell him what he wants to know. Trouble is, what he wants to know hasn't happened yet. <br /><br />Em and Finn have a shared past, but no future unless they can find a way out. The present is torture - being kept apart, overhearing each other's anguish as the Doctor relentlessly seeks answers. There's no way back from here, to what they used to be, the world they used to know. Then Em finds a note in her cell which changes everything. It's from her future self and contains some simple but very clear instructions. Em must travel back in time to avert a tragedy that's about to unfold. Worse, she has to pursue and kill the boy she loves to change the future.</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_470031248" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/470031248" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/470031248?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408835197" href="/book/show/17451105-all-our-yesterdays">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer470031248" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2576837417047121537"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>I'm still reeling from this book. I finished it with that sad, hollow feeling that makes it impossible to read anything else for a while because you're still living in the book's world and still caught up in the adventures of those characters. And I didn't expect to like this book anywhere near as much as I did. It's a science-fiction book with a romance that is central to the story and we all know <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/230348011' rel='nofollow noopener'>how</a> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/240209169' rel='nofollow noopener'>well</a> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/183217980' rel='nofollow noopener'>those</a> go. But it's well-written and compelling with a very interesting and seemingly </span>
  <span id="freeText2576837417047121537" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>I'm still reeling from this book. I finished it with that sad, hollow feeling that makes it impossible to read anything else for a while because you're still living in the book's world and still caught up in the adventures of those characters. And I didn't expect to like this book anywhere near as much as I did. It's a science-fiction book with a romance that is central to the story and we all know <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/230348011" rel="nofollow noopener">how</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/240209169" rel="nofollow noopener">well</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/183217980" rel="nofollow noopener">those</a> go. But it's well-written and compelling with a very interesting and seemingly original (to me) take on the concept and science behind time travel. It took me longer than usual to read this book; but sometimes it does take me more time to read books I really loved because I tend to savour them a bit more. I find myself pausing to read sentences again because I liked them so much, or because the emotions I feel are too much to process in one reading.<br><br>Some people might be tempted to call this book a dystopia, which is fair enough because it is about a future world gone horribly wrong, but I view books about time travel (especially ones as scientifically detailed as this) to be the more traditional brand of sci-fi. Though, for me, it still carries that key ingredient that I look for in a dystopia, that key ingredient that has had me spending many disappointed hours searching through the dystopian craze for a book that holds it. It's an element I've been addicted to for a very long time. When I was eleven I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5471.Nineteen_Eighty_Four" title="Nineteen Eighty-Four by George Orwell" rel="nofollow noopener">Nineteen Eighty-Four</a> and then when I was fourteen I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38447.The_Handmaid_s_Tale" title="The Handmaid's Tale by Margaret Atwood" rel="nofollow noopener">The Handmaid's Tale</a> - these two readings sparked a thus-far lifelong interest in a future world that, no matter how realistic or unrealistic, is so well-crafted and well-explained that it's impossible to not believe in it. A world that you can see happening because the author shows how we got from here to there. They base it in science and facts and politics to make it seem like a very real possibility and to make you absolutely terrified from start to finish.<br><br>This book scared me. Ms Terrill managed to convince me completely that time travel was not only real, but a very real threat to the life we know. Think about it. What could a government do with time travel? What alliances could they break apart before they ever happened? What foreign powers could they destroy before they ever rose up against them? And I know what people will think - there's a time paradox, right? You change the past and then you change the future. But Terrill also offers a very interesting and convincing explanation for that. I've always been a bit of a nerd, but not so much a science nerd until I read the scientific foundations of this story with wide-eyed awe. Maybe it couldn't really work like that. No, <i>probably</i> it couldn't really work like that. But isn't that the definition of good science fiction? To take the impossible or the improbable and convince the reader that it's real?<br><br>Let's move onto the characters. They are so multi-layered and complex that they jump off the page. One of the things I loved the most was seeing Em as she is now, Marina as she was then and seeing how one could grow into the other. The growth of her character felt realistic, you could easily see how her experiences had changed her and the book touches upon the question of how much people can really change. How much of our adult selves lurks beneath the surface when we are children? If we do bad things, when did we become a person capable of doing bad things? Was it always there? This is such a fascinating book on so many levels - the science-y world-building aspect, the political aspect and the characters' struggles. But, above all, I adored Finn. And maybe that's why I don't care that the romance played quite a big part in this book, because Finn is fantastic. And funny. And wonderful. And I want a Finn too!<br><br>The main questions this book asks are: if you could go back and kill a man who would do terrible things before he had the power to do so, would you? What if that person was one you loved? How easy would it be to look into the eyes of an innocent who couldn't believe they'd ever hurt anyone... and pull the trigger? Is that person even the same as the one they'll become? This book not only scared me, it broke my heart too. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399741ra/773903.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And that ending, oh god, <i>that ending</i>. Perfect bittersweetness.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="2576837417047121537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="&quot;That&#39;s All&quot; Ash" class="user" itemprop="url" name="&quot;That&#39;s All&quot; Ash" href="/user/show/5606933-that-s-all-ash">&quot;That&#39;s All&quot; Ash</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer717362094" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12550953855767690080">I think this is the first time I’ve written a bad review for a 4-star book.<br/><br/>Is that even Goodreads-legal?<br/><br/>Here’s my problem with <b>All Our Yesterdays</b>: It was awesome… <i>once I got past the beginning</i>.<br/><br/>This was my status update at 17%:<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i> ‘Okie dokie. So. This is a dystopian book about a girl who’s already lived fourteen (fifteen?) lives and needs to get to a time machine so that she can jump forward to her past and it’s also a dual POV between her current self and her past self and the relationship with</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText12550953855767690080" style="display:none">I think this is the first time I’ve written a bad review for a 4-star book.<br><br>Is that even Goodreads-legal?<br><br>Here’s my problem with <b>All Our Yesterdays</b>: It was awesome… <i>once I got past the beginning</i>.<br><br>This was my status update at 17%:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i> ‘Okie dokie. So. This is a dystopian book about a girl who’s already lived fourteen (fifteen?) lives and needs to get to a time machine so that she can jump forward to her past and it’s also a dual POV between her current self and her past self and the relationship with the boy who she now loves and hated back then.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/original1.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380436324ra/881858.gif" alt=" photo original1.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Are you tired yet?<br><br><b>And that’s just what I could describe using only 420 characters.</b><br><br><u>And I’m like:</u><br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/tumblr_m6ftqkHG3N1rwcc6bo1_500.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380436324ra/881859.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_m6ftqkHG3N1rwcc6bo1_500.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>***<b>Seriously, lady… why not just sell your book with a bottle of vodka, a Rubik’s cube, and a hand-written note that says, “Good luck.” while you’re at it?</b>*** <br><br><i>Fuuuuuck.</i><br><br><br>♦<i>
  <u>
    <b>The Good Thing About This Book</b>
  </u>
</i>♦<br><br>It <b>does</b> have a beautiful story. And I know I probably scared you off about the beginning and all that… but honestly, when you get your footing with everything; it’s kind of amazing!<br><br><b>It’s about a girl who has to go back in time to kill someone who at one point, meant the <i>world</i> to her. But horrible things happen to that person, and that person becomes something menacing and a danger to mankind because he or she (I’m trying not to spoil it for you) invents something that shouldn’t have been invented. Because he or she wants to use it for reasons that would destroy everything.<br><br>And the reason why that girl has lived fourteen or fifteen lives is because she keeps failing at killing him or her. Because this is a person she has loved, does love, and always will love.</b><br><br>So I say read this book.<br><br>But use this:<br><br><b>---&gt;</b><u>
  <i>
    <b>◊ Ash’s Chapter One Cheat Sheet ◊</b>
  </i>
</u><b>&lt;---</b><br><br><u>#1.</u> “<b>Cassandra</b>” is the time machine. *I*, for a good 15% of the book, thought it was a town. Or a bartender. (At this point in the story, I was kind of leaning towards the bartender. Because seriously? That’s what *I* needed.)<br><br><b>It’s not.</b> <br>It’s the time machine.<br><br>So when the characters are running around in the first chapter yelling things like, “We have to get to Cassandra!” <i>it’s because they have to get to <i>the time machine.</i><br><br><u>#2.</u> This book has a dual POV between Em and Marina. So when the POV suddenly changes from Em <b>to</b> Marina; and you happen to be like me: and you’re thinking as you come across Marina’s POV: “Who in the fuckety fuck is <b>Marina</b>?!” (because it’s not explained before the POV shift)<br><br><b>*Answer</b>: <i>Marina</i> is Em. Four years ago.<b>*</b> <br><br><u>#3</u>. When Em gets that note that says, “You have to kill him.”… it means the doctor. (And no; I’m still not spoiling anything by telling you) Okay? You would figure it out later, but I wish *I* would have known that sooner. So that’s why I’m telling you.<br><br><u>#4.</u> Pay close attention to James.<br><br><br><b><u>That’s all.</u></b><br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/tumblr_m5idojf1ut1rssa6wo1_500.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380436324ra/881860.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_m5idojf1ut1rssa6wo1_500.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br></i></span>

<div id="review_1397163004" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1397163004" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1397163004?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Recommended for fans of stories about time travel and romance. ^^ </span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Aj the Ravenous Reader by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/7366569-fafa-s-book-corner">Fafa&#39;s Book Corner</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1397163004" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16448751762997266869"><br/><b> 3 to 3.5 stars </b><br/><br/>I’m both impressed and disappointed. Impressed because I had no idea this was going to be about time travel so it was a complete surprise because the concept (Marina and Finn try to save the world by going four years back to the past to kill their best friend, James aka Doctor who invented the machine that will allow people to time travel that consequently will cause the world’s doom) is quite unique. I’m a bit disappointed because I honestly thought this was going to be an actio</span>
  <span id="freeText16448751762997266869" style="display:none"><br><b> 3 to 3.5 stars </b><br><br>I’m both impressed and disappointed. Impressed because I had no idea this was going to be about time travel so it was a complete surprise because the concept (Marina and Finn try to save the world by going four years back to the past to kill their best friend, James aka Doctor who invented the machine that will allow people to time travel that consequently will cause the world’s doom) is quite unique. I’m a bit disappointed because I honestly thought this was going to be an action-packed dystopian novel which I’m really eager for at the moment. :/<br><br>I enjoyed the story like I would a sci-fi movie about time travel. It would have been so much better if I liked the actors. :/ Perhaps if I read this 365 yesterdays ago, I would have loved it! Now however, I couldn’t seem to connect much with the heroine and the hero (also the antihero) and that’s when I struggle most in reading. It could have a really good plot but if I couldn’t feel the characters, it usually ends just okay for me. Good thing there’s another hero- Finn, the only character I loved and the main reason I enjoyed the entire story. <br><br>Those opening and closing chapters were the best but honestly, there were maybe three to four chapters in the middle which I skimmed because the alternating POVs of the future and the present Marina couldn’t hold my one hundred percent attention. The entire time travel concept although very imaginative was a bit blurry for me. The characters kept talking about how bad the world has become because of time travel but I wanted more proof. I wanted a clearer picture of that world. Or maybe I’m just bitter that most of my friends have already read and loved this and this is my own little way of revenge. (Feeling this villainous vibe.)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442801260ra/16280423.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Kidding! Lol. <br><br>The events toward the end were really intense and impressive and those were the parts where I was completely attentive and where the other characters finally earned my empathy. It was heartbreaking! In the end though, I think, what were mainly resolved were the main characters’ personal issues and paradoxes. <br><br>Still a good read though, still a good read so please, don’t rely too much on this review because I have a strong feeling that this is a “it’s not you book, it’s me” case. Also, I would lurve to see a movie version! <br><br>Thanks to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1319319661?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Fatima's five star review</a> that encouraged me to read the book. Do check out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1113649365?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Rachel's awesome review</a> too. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16448751762997266869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=august">august</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer313591333" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15314756838209368418"><b>3.5 stars</b> <br/><br/>I liked how the author addressed time travel paradox and causal loop questions, but I felt less enthused about the characters. <br/><br/><i>Full text of review may be found in <a href='http://www.themidnightgarden.net/2013/08/allouryesterdays.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Midnight Garden</a>.   <span id="freeText13173247167207917556" style="display:none">I’m offended. <br><br>I don’t know what this book was actually trying to do but all it accomplished was just to compound the thinking that <b>‘if you need something done, do not send teenagers to do it’.</b>I’m not a teenager by any means, but come <i>ON</i>, they deserve better representation than this.<br><br>*smh*<br><br>It failed at ‘thrilling’ since most of the book <i>kept focusing on the ‘wrong’ things.</i> Like why are we spending so much time listening to these clueless characters having a back and forth on the same old things over and over?? We found out from the very first scene Marina appeared, basically the first page she was in, that she <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[was totally, absolutely in luvvv with James <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and 250 pages later, we’re STILL talking about this? We already KNOW. Don’t you have more important things to tell us?? I thought it’s imperative to fucking save the world, right?<br><br>Then I saw this.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Marina: “Nobody loves me, and why should they?”</i>

When the book was just in contemporary timeline like when they were so desperate to avoid the mob of press that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[they went to a ‘bad side’ of town to stay at a house that’s never been vetted/secured even though someone just tried to kill James? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Really now? <div id="review_697853303" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/697853303" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/697853303?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=2nd-favorites">2nd-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=read-on-kindle">read-on-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=five-stars">five-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=own-electronic">own-electronic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer697853303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5403281123133670519"><i>All Our Yesterdays</i> made me:<br/>- grip my Kindle so hard it left an imprint on my forehead<br/>- whisper-scream in anticipation and outrage<br/>- believe in its time-traveling, dystopian premise<br/>- cry soft tears that landed in my orange juice<br/>- drink my own tears (see above)<br/>- wish I had read it so much sooner<br/><br/>I have so much love for this book, my first five-star read of 2015. It centers on Em, a young woman stuck in a cell with nothing besides the voice of a boy in the cell next to hers and a list of instructions</span>
  <span id="freeText5403281123133670519" style="display:none"><i>All Our Yesterdays</i> made me:<br />- grip my Kindle so hard it left an imprint on my forehead<br />- whisper-scream in anticipation and outrage<br />- believe in its time-traveling, dystopian premise<br />- cry soft tears that landed in my orange juice<br />- drink my own tears (see above)<br />- wish I had read it so much sooner<br /><br />I have so much love for this book, my first five-star read of 2015. It centers on Em, a young woman stuck in a cell with nothing besides the voice of a boy in the cell next to hers and a list of instructions she finds inside a drain. She has made multiple attempts to stop the creation of a time machine that will destroy the world, but every try has landed her in the same position: trapped and tortured in a cell by the man called the doctor.<br /><br />Meanwhile, Marina, a rich, insecure girl who goes to a private school, has fallen in love with her handsome and intellectual neighbor James. But when James loses it all one night, Marina must fight to save both him and herself. Soon, Em and Marina's stories intertwine in a way that leaves both of them reeling.<br /><br />I finished <i>All Our Yesterdays</i> in less than 24 hours, and I would have swallowed it whole in a second if I could have. Cristin Terrill writes with intensity and purpose. Every scene contained well-paced action, deft characterization, and snappy dialogue. She balances a tricky concept with a neat set of characters, and both her world and its inhabitants made sense. The development of Marina, Em, Finn, and even James left me in awe, and the bittersweet ending of <i>All Our Yesterdays</i> pierced my heart in the best possible way.<br /><br />I cannot recommend this book enough, in particular to fans of YA fiction of any genre. While I feel unsure on whether I want a sequel to this book - it works so well as a single volume - I hope I have the opportunity to read more of Terrill's writing in the future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5403281123133670519" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_930405356" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/930405356" />
    <a title="Christine Wallflower &amp; Dark Romance Junkie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie"><img alt="Christine Wallflower &amp; Dark Romance Junkie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505392311p2/11641363.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/930405356?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine Wallflower &amp; Dark Romance Junkie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine Wallflower &amp; Dark Romance Junkie " href="/user/show/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie">Christine Wallflower &amp; Dark Romance Junkie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781408835203" href="/book/show/18210450-all-our-yesterdays">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie?shelf=thriller-suspense">thriller-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie?shelf=give-this-author-a-bells">give-this-author-a-bells</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie?shelf=fantasy-and-magic">fantasy-and-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie?shelf=crime-mystery">crime-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie?shelf=bloody-love-triangle">bloody-love-triangle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer930405356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3721320799536219842"><b>4.5 Stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399653933i/9578998.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>HOLY SHIT ON A STICK, WHAT THE HELL DID I JUST READ!!!</b><br/><br/>Yes, yes I know it's a really amazing sci-fi,time travel thriller, that's chocka-blocked full of action and suspense and a liberal dose of angsty teen love. This I know, but my reaction towards the story completely surprised me!<br/><br/>Firstly if you plan on reading this book, here's a tip: Keep your wits about you, there's so much going on and every detail is so important, you can't miss anything! Secondly. OMG about halfway through this bo</span>
  <span id="freeText3721320799536219842" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Stars</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399653933i/9578998.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>HOLY SHIT ON A STICK, WHAT THE HELL DID I JUST READ!!!</b><br><br>Yes, yes I know it's a really amazing sci-fi,time travel thriller, that's chocka-blocked full of action and suspense and a liberal dose of angsty teen love. This I know, but my reaction towards the story completely surprised me!<br><br>Firstly if you plan on reading this book, here's a tip: Keep your wits about you, there's so much going on and every detail is so important, you can't miss anything! Secondly. OMG about halfway through this book I was getting major Butterfly Effect vibes, not even vibes they were freaking quakes! I loved Butterfly Effect! Look, I mean the stories are completely different, it's the entire feel of the book and certain scenes made me think of the movie.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399713921ra/9586066.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The story has three main characters. There's Marina our heroine, she's been in love with James since she was in diapers (well almost) she's constantly pining over him like any hormonal teenaged girl would. In the beginning of the story, she annoyed so bad I second guessed my decision on reading this book, she was spoiled, bratty and had serious self esteem problems. But trust me her faults are vital to the story, Marina does some serious growing up over a short period of time. Her transformation is fundamental to the story. <br><br>Then there's James. a child prodigy, he's busy studying to get his PHD in God knows what, he's a brain, that's all you need to understand.<br>He's also this really awkward kid, who got really good looking overnight, and hasn't adjusted to his new image. You see, his older brother Nate is a congressman, and these attributes give his "popularity" a major boost. But ultimately he's still the same gangly nerd who couldn't fit in. He also has behavioral problems...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399713921ra/9586067.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>And finally we have, Finn, the oddball in the lot. He's background isn't as affluent as Marina's and James. He's James' best friend and the bane of Marina's existence, because wherever James is, Finn is there too. And how the hell is Marina supposed to get James' to notice her if Finn keeps getting in the way??? *insert eyeroll* Finn is sweet, quirky and the cutest this under the sun and I absolutely loved him! No matter how horrible his situation is he never let it show, and he always cracked a joke.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399711092i/9585809.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>***WARNING***</b><br>I'm about to get all cheezy and teary eyed. This book will evoke intense emotions, feels! Forget about the fact that is science fiction and dystopian and just read the story. It's unforgettable, keeps you wondering right till the end and then some. It's a coming of age story in a really weird and warped way. I didn't give you any details about the actual plot because I feel like all of that would spoil. Seriously, if I was to write a detailed review, it would take me days, that's how intricate the plot is!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399714619i/9586150.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="3721320799536219842" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_633982493" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/633982493" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/633982493?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer633982493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13381400777622522038">There's been a slew of time travel books lately and <i>All Our Yesterdays</i> is another one that I can add on the short list of those that impressed me. The time travel concept introduced, while hard to grasp like any and all time travel science, explains how paradoxes fixes itself in a manner that's utterly fascinating, while giving us a plot that is both thought-provoking and exciting.<br/><br/><i>All Our Yesterdays</i> has a past/present setting that involves a unique double characterization; even though our main c</span>
  <span id="freeText13381400777622522038" style="display:none">There's been a slew of time travel books lately and <i>All Our Yesterdays</i> is another one that I can add on the short list of those that impressed me. The time travel concept introduced, while hard to grasp like any and all time travel science, explains how paradoxes fixes itself in a manner that's utterly fascinating, while giving us a plot that is both thought-provoking and exciting.<br><br><i>All Our Yesterdays</i> has a past/present setting that involves a unique double characterization; even though our main character is a singular person, both her younger and older self form the dual POV of this novel which I found especially interesting. Marina can be hard on herself; even though she admits to turning heads, she doesn't think she's pretty or anything special. I didn't connect to Marina right away because this attitude kept me at arm's length, but her caring heart does grow on you. Em is more my kind of gal with her strong will and tough attitude. She is just as caring, if not more, and having learned to love herself makes her personality more attractive. Because of this hardened shell, both narratives are considerably different, though with a likeness at their core. Each perspective introduces a set of secondary characters with which the protagonist has a peculiar bond. It was striking to see the changes in their relationships as the story progressed. Finn became my favorite side character, but James's exceptional intelligence and obvious instability had me compelled. With a dual narrative consisting of past and present characters, it allowed for twists to be dropped at regular intervals which unveiled the mysteries of what happened in the future that changed everything to such a degree. These almost always caught me off guard and often shone a new light on certain characters.<br><br>Romantically, this novel contains a unique spin. I can't divulge very much, but we see how one love crumbles and how one flourishes. It's kind of bittersweet at times, but I loved how it turned out in the end. Even though its presence is constant, and its role integral to the story, the romance never overpowers the plot; it's fused into its roots. The book as a whole is well paced with the right amount of suspense and tension. The described political controls of the future are realistic under the circumstances, raising moral questions while at it. Once or twice, to make the plot move forward the author uses opportune happenings that required a little forgiveness on my part. As an example, after Marina gets nothing but a few alphabetical letters from Nate, she has it all figured out and everyone's quick to agree to a goose chase based on this vague thread of information. However, these instances are insignificant in the grand scheme of things and I still consider the plot to be solid. As for the ending, I had to re-read it and think for a bit for it to make sense. I may not even be correct in my interpretation, either way it makes for a good time travel paradox discussion.<br><br>With flawless writing and an unwavering pace, Cristin has weaved time-travel, romance, political intrigue, and mystery into this page-turner of a novel!<br><br>--<br><i>An advance copy was provided by the publisher for review.</i><br><br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380236618i/681468.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13381400777622522038" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_558913609" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/558913609" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/558913609?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=arc-galley-or-author">arc-galley-or-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=alternating-pov">alternating-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=standalone">standalone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=best-of">best-of</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer558913609" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5985196470930542351">Oh my! This is what a true time travel story should be about.<br/><br/><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/cristin-terrill/review-all-our-yesterdays.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413057i/812842.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>The suspense, the confusion, the puzzled pieces that start to fit together, the world building, the character development (both in the past and the future)… Should I really tell you how much I loved this story?<br/>It was absolutely AMAZING! It blew my mind, of course I loved it!<br/><br/>I’d spend all my yesterdays reading this book only to feel this joy with which it filled my heart, because there’s nothing better than finding a new favorite bo</span>
  <span id="freeText5985196470930542351" style="display:none">Oh my! This is what a true time travel story should be about.<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/cristin-terrill/review-all-our-yesterdays.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413057i/812842.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The suspense, the confusion, the puzzled pieces that start to fit together, the world building, the character development (both in the past and the future)… Should I really tell you how much I loved this story?<br>It was absolutely AMAZING! It blew my mind, of course I loved it!<br><br>I’d spend all my yesterdays reading this book only to feel this joy with which it filled my heart, because there’s nothing better than finding a new favorite book – and this one here is a keeper.<br><br><b>TIME TRAVEL:</b><br><br>I love the concept of time traveling, still it’s usually hard to find a good book that touches this subject. So, why “All Our Yesterdays” worked for me you wonder?<br><br>Well, it doesn’t spend a lot of time explaining how things work, but the details it gives seem believable. Also, the connection between present and past is really strong – the characters are completely different now, you see how time has changed them, but you also feel the need to see why is it that they changed so much, how wrong did things turn out for them in the time between, and how the future selves might make things better.<br><br>The decisions are hard to make, the plans go wrong more than right, there are turnarounds after turnarounds and even though you might feel that things don’t add up, in the end you will see that they actually do.<br>Did I tell you how much I loved this story?! Oh, my!<br><br><b>PLOT:</b><br><br>My incoherent book description (also called ‘babbling in my new love language’):<br><i>Run before the future catches up with you;<br>Hide between your yesterdays until you make it right;<br>Fight for a version of yourself that might chase to exist.<br>… It’s all worth it, because when the past and the future collide and you’re running out of time there is only one thing holding it all up: hope!<br>And maybe, just maybe, that will be enough.</i><br><br>I’ll keep it at that, not wanting to spoil anything for you, but be assured that the action keeps you on the edge of your seat at ALL times, switching back and forth between time perspectives, only making you want more from both of them.<br><br><b>CHARACTERS:</b><br><br>I liked how all <a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/cristin-terrill/review-all-our-yesterdays.html#characters" rel="nofollow noopener">the characters</a> developed over the time.<br>They kept consistent, even though there is this innocence that has been lost in the past years. You see how strong they are now, how weak and naive they’ve been in the past and you wish to find more about the things that made them change that much. But at heart, they are just the same; they wish for the same things, they fight for the same reasons, only at a different level.<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396274066i/9108998.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <i>Time is coming for us, and coming fast.</i>
</blockquote><br>What I loved the most is that the characters are flawed, they make mistakes, but they have also depth; they fight for the right things, but they still have a heart to lead them. They seem real and they question the things they need to do, they fear the possibility failure (they can even accept it) and they simply want to make things better for each of them. I loved them all and it pained me to see how unfair life can be sometimes, and how easily some beautiful things can break into thousands of pieces just in an instant.<br><br><b>CONCLUSION:</b><br><br>Where do I preorder this? Because I want it on my bedstand next to a few other beloved stories.<br><br>Think <a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/elizabeth-norris/review-unraveling.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Unraveling</a> (with the fast pacing and the mind-blowing turnarounds), <a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/kasie-west/review-pivot-point.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Pivot Point</a> (because of the two perspectives) and <a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/beth-revis/across-the-universe-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Across the Universe</a> (sorry, but I will keep this to myself) – all in one.<br><br>If I were to be really honest with myself I would give this book 4.5 stars because the future didn’t change as quickly as the characters interacted with the present and I wasn’t really sure why was that (it gave me some sort of unsettling feeling). The theory might work even so, but I feel like the future could have been altered just a bit by some events.. maybe. And also, once or twice the characters’ reactions were a bit slow, they made the connections between facts really slow and I even felt smarter then them (not that I complain, but I wanted to yell at them to just open their eyes, LOL).<br><br>But these are some very minor things, I loved this book to pieces – loved the action, the suspense, the romance.. everything. And guess what, this is a debut novel – and if the first one is this good, I am keeping my eyes on you, dear Cristin!<br><br>Happy midnight reading!<br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/cristin-terrill/review-all-our-yesterdays.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334106i/693595.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i> * This review can also be found at <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/cristin-terrill/review-all-our-yesterdays.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a> <br>** ARC received from the publisher for review - Thank you!</i><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________<br></span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1442503941016658606">See more reviews at <a href='http://theyabooklover.blogspot.com.au/' rel='nofollow noopener'>YA Midnight Reads</a><br/><br/><b>Thank you Bloomsbury for sending me this copy. No compensation was given or taken to alter this review. </b> <br/><br/><i>'But it's the last line that makes me scramble for the toilet in the corner of my cell. <br/><b>You have to kill him.'</b></i> <br/><br/>I guess it's no lie that I am an absolute stingy person when it comes to giving out 5 stars. To me, they are the rarest gems of the pile. Being this, I believe I should be permitted to just throw confetti across the room and say, "READ THIS BOOK A</span>
  <span id="freeText1442503941016658606" style="display:none">See more reviews at <a href="http://theyabooklover.blogspot.com.au/" rel="nofollow noopener">YA Midnight Reads</a><br /><br /><b>Thank you Bloomsbury for sending me this copy. No compensation was given or taken to alter this review. </b> <br /><br /><i>'But it's the last line that makes me scramble for the toilet in the corner of my cell. <br /><b>You have to kill him.'</b></i> <br /><br />I guess it's no lie that I am an absolute stingy person when it comes to giving out 5 stars. To me, they are the rarest gems of the pile. Being this, I believe I should be permitted to just throw confetti across the room and say, "READ THIS BOOK AND I WILL LOVE YOU AND YOU WILL LOVE ME! It's a double deal!" So that's what I'll do. With a death threat added to the end, don't forget. But of course, if you cannot resist my awesomeness, read on. <br /><br />All Our Yesterdays broke me, tore me into shreds. I'm still shocked. I'm still dazed. I'm still mind bended into awkward places. I'm still shipping James and Marina. And I'm still clasping onto Em and Finn's hands, not letting go. All Our Yesterdays burned into my stomach, churned a hole that's still there. Entwined with assassination attacks, politics, romance, strong characters and an enormous amount of imagination, Cristin Terrill debut is not to be missed and will sweep readers off their feet. Miss out on this novel and you will regret it. <br /><br />A brief summary of this novel is that we have three main characters, who in which create six main characters in all. Don't get it? Good. Otherwise you'll be hunting me down if I explained any further. The book opens up to Em, who's closest neighbour is Finn, fellow imprisoned victim, with desperate searches for escape, Em finds a list. It's full, and all have been crossed out except one. She has told herself to kill her past love. To save the world. To save herself. Utterly suspenseful till the last page, All Our Yesterdays can also hint about another paradoxically ambiguous question, how does each action affect our future? Our tomorrows?<br /><br />With really only three main characters, Terrill accomplishes well with her limited selection. All I couldn't help but grow to admire. There is Em, who's narration is one of determination, humour and heart. James, reserved and complete nerd. And Finn, oh Finn, sweet, sarcastic and wholly deep. The way these three developed together and unravelled the story was captivating, I could truly feel emotions reflecting off their eyes into mine. So genuine and heart breaking.<br /><br />All Our Yesterdays may be plot driven, however our subplot unequivocally stands with the friendship and romances illustrated. Craftily and conducted with fantastic dynamics, Terrill clearly knows what she's doing, it's magnificent beyond words. While there is a hint of a love triangle, my usual rush of eye rolls did not appear due to how complex this relationship was and how, at the same time, was just a trio of best friends. While Em, Finn and James may not all get it their way in the end, giggles erupted and tears were shed. The depth of the connections in All Our Yesterdays simply can't be further pressed upon. <br /><br />In terms of world building and wiring, Terrill has excelled. I didn't feel blind when reading this novel- I could construct the world that Terrill set as a foundation- I could sense the wider image sharper and more concise, the details and information of this This sci-fi, war tainted world wasn't dumped but slowly shredded, so strategically. All Our Yesterdays' writing is something to be commended for. It's heart breaking and confronting. Raw and loving. Terrill's writing is chilling, scaring and completely beautiful. <br /><br />A well plotted and drawn world with a fantastic handful of characters, All Our Yesterdays overwhelmed me with epicness. The writing was bold and raw, the world was dark and hopeful. For a debut, Cristin Terrill shows an ambitious set of work and I will be sure to read her future novels. And like I said at the beginning, read this!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1442503941016658606" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_635483458" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/635483458" />
    <a title="Scarlet" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3839903-scarlet"><img alt="Scarlet" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556098025p2/3839903.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/635483458?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scarlet" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scarlet" href="/user/show/3839903-scarlet">Scarlet</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408835197" href="/book/show/17451105-all-our-yesterdays">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3839903-scarlet?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3839903-scarlet?shelf=impressive-debuts">impressive-debuts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3839903-scarlet?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3839903-scarlet?shelf=best-of-ya">best-of-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer635483458" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4643873981389890582">Is it just me or does <i>All Our Yesterdays</i> have a distinctly cinematic flavor? I feel like I've just sat through a fast-paced movie about time travel and two people on the run trying to save the world. I'm not sure if that's a good thing but it kept me interested and intrigued till the very end, which is more than I can say about most YA books. And considering this is a debut, I'd say that's an impressive accomplishment.<br/><br/>Em and Finn escape from a prison cell and travel 4 years back in time to preve</span>
  <span id="freeText4643873981389890582" style="display:none">Is it just me or does <i>All Our Yesterdays</i> have a distinctly cinematic flavor? I feel like I've just sat through a fast-paced movie about time travel and two people on the run trying to save the world. I'm not sure if that's a good thing but it kept me interested and intrigued till the very end, which is more than I can say about most YA books. And considering this is a debut, I'd say that's an impressive accomplishment.<br /><br />Em and Finn escape from a prison cell and travel 4 years back in time to prevent the world from becoming what it has due to the misuse of time travel. This is their 14th attempt to save the world, and their plan this time is to kill the "doctor" who invented the time machine. But the doctor in the future is their best friend in the past. So Em and Finn are actually on a mission to kill someone they both once loved, and in some small measure, still do.<br /><br /><b>The things that stand out in <i>All Our Yesterdays</i> are pacing, characters and plot, in that order.</b><br /><br /><br /><u>Pacing</u>:<br />The chapters are alternately narrated by Em, who has come from the future, and Marina, who is the younger version of Em in the present time zone. Em knows everything that Marina is yet to find out so by constantly switching from one to another, <b>Terrill not only manages to reveal the story one piece at a time but also builds up a mad sense of urgency</b>. I was never bored while reading and even when the romance bits were underway, the pace did not dwindle.<br /><br /><br /><u>Characters</u>:<br />Having the future and present versions of the same character in the same frame carries the risk of creating a disconnect between them. But Terrill's protagonists are just so well-etched. <b>As different as Marina is from Em, I could tell they were both the same person</b> with individual perspectives warped by time. This also applies to Finn, who, irrespective of time-zones, is a complete sweetheart.<br /><br />The only character I had issues with is James a.k.a the doctor. While the James we meet is a complicated young boy, he's also drastically different from the future version, who only appears toward the end. I'm not convinced someone can change so much in 4 years.<br /><br /><br /><u>Plot</u>:<br />The plot is pretty ambitious for YA and a little far-fetched (for starters, you must assume that all security personnel are stupid enough to be continuously outsmarted by a bunch of teenagers) but I liked it. <b>Time travel is not used as a mere plot gimmick in the story, it <i>is</i> the story</b>. Even though there is a fair bit of romance, it does not out-weigh the sci-fi element.<br /><br />However, the plot focuses only on the present and the future. What happens in between is not explained. Just like I don't see how James could possibly become the doctor, I don't get how the world could possibly change so much in 4 measly years. <br /><br />There are many brain-bending paradoxes about time that I'm sure must have holes but I'm too intimidated to try and explore them. It took me some effort just to understand the ending. The thing with time-travel is that it's hypothetical. We don't know how it works. How do you fault the kind of logic that doesn't exist?<br /><br /><br />Overall, <i>All Our Yesterdays</i> was an exciting read and one of the better YA sci-fi offerings this year. It definitely works as a standalone, so I don't see the need for a sequel. <br /> <br /><b>3.5 well-earned stars for an impressive debut.</b><br /><br /><br /><i>*With thanks to Netgalley for the free digital copy*</i></span>
