    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_693920015" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/693920015" />
    <a title="Brigid ✩" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/886144-brigid"><img alt="Brigid ✩" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581869052p2/886144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/693920015?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brigid ✩" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brigid ✩" href="/user/show/886144-brigid">Brigid ✩</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=on-my-kindle">on-my-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=crime-and-mystery">crime-and-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=yes-yes-yes">yes-yes-yes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer693920015" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4924348736676082561"><b>Thank you to NetGalley and Disney Hyperion for providing me with an ARC of this book!</b><br/><br/><b>Actual rating: 4.5 Stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"Is that breakthrough what you were going to tell me about?" I say. "The night you came home?"<br/><br/>James nods but doesn't look away from the road. "Yeah."<br/><br/>"What is it?" Finn asks. <br/><br/>"It's something I've been working on for a long time. I'm finally starting to make some real progress, and those pages there are the crux of my formulations."<br/><br/>"What are they for?"<br/><br/>"Travel in the fourth dimension."<br/><br/>"Hu</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText4924348736676082561" style="display:none"><b>Thank you to NetGalley and Disney Hyperion for providing me with an ARC of this book!</b><br><br><b>Actual rating: 4.5 Stars</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Is that breakthrough what you were going to tell me about?" I say. "The night you came home?"<br><br>James nods but doesn't look away from the road. "Yeah."<br><br>"What is it?" Finn asks. <br><br>"It's something I've been working on for a long time. I'm finally starting to make some real progress, and those pages there are the crux of my formulations."<br><br>"What are they for?"<br><br>"Travel in the fourth dimension."<br><br>"Huh?"<br><br>James's gaze flicks into the rearview mirror and back again. "Time travel."<br><br>I've listened to James talk about this for years, so it doesn't faze me, but Finn clicks off his seat belt and scoots up between us. "Say what now?"<br><br>"I know it sounds ridiculous, but I think it's possible and Dr. Feinberg agrees. When I finish those formulas, I'll prove it."<br><br>James's fingers tighten around the steering wheel until his knuckles turn white. His passion has always been one of the things I love most about him, but it worries me, too. I've learned a lot about James these last two days, and I see more than ever now how he's like forged metal, strong but brittle, unable to bend.<br><br>"What happens when you prove it?" Finn asks.<br><br>"We fix the world."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>Summary:</b><br><br>Em is trapped in a secret military base, where she has suffered through interrogation and torture for what seems like forever. A note she finds taped inside the drain––a note in her own hand––informs her that she has been through numerous attempts to avoid this situation and to destroy a time machine that has gravely endangered the world. After all these attempts, it seems she only has one choice: to kill the time machine's creator.<br><br>The only problem is that the boy who invented the time machine is her childhood best friend, James. The two of them grew up next door to each other, and as they grew older and became closer, they began to develop strong feelings for each other. But when a devastating tragedy changed James's life forever, things began to fall apart––leading to James becoming a completely different person with some terrible intentions.<br><br>Em knows she may have to do something horrible to prevent James's invention––but if she doesn't, James's plans may lead to widespread paranoia that will drastically change the world.<br><br><b>My thoughts:</b><br><br>When I first read this, I rated it 4 stars. But after thinking about it for a few months (I know, I know––I'm so behind on reviews), I've bumped it up to a 4.5. It's not quite a 5 for me, but it is a really good book and one of the most memorable things I've read in a while. <br><br><i>All Our Yesterdays</i> really blind-sided me. I saw a few fellow reviewers posting things about it, and when I looked it up I thought it sounded like it might be cool, but I didn't plan on reading it unless I got an ARC of it. As it turned out, I did get one. So, I figured I would give it a shot. Before I read it, I'd read a few other ARCs from NetGalley that had been really disappointing, so to be honest I wasn't expecting much. Starting out, I thought this seemed like a pretty typical dystopian book of some sort; I didn't really know what I was getting myself into.<br><br>I was pleasantly surprised. <i>Very</i> pleasantly surprised.<br><br>I found the story confusing at first. There are two storylines (kind of)––one from the point of view of Em, the other from her former/alternate self, Marina. In other words, they're the same girl but in different … times? Dimensions? Whatever, hopefully you get what I mean.<br><br>It was all pretty unclear to me at first, but once I got more into the story it all started to piece together. And once it did, I was really hooked. Somehow, I unexpectedly found myself very engaged in the story and characters. It may seem like a typical sci-fi movie plot on the surface, but I actually found it quite thought-provoking and emotional. I was surprised that, by the end, I was nearly in tears.<br><br>It's kind of hard to explain what was so interesting and powerful about this story, especially because it's pretty complicated. But basically, I thought it took a somewhat clichéd concept and made it very original and memorable, with complex characters and a riveting pace. It wasn't perfect and there were still some things I didn't quite understand, but I thought it was a great book over all. <br><br><b>
  <u>What I liked:</u>
</b><br><br>- It's difficult to write a book about time-travel without making it horribly confusing. And although I was pretty mystified when I started the book, as it went along I felt that the author was able to handle the complex issues of time-travel pretty well. Although in the end there was some weird paradox stuff that I wasn't sure quite made sense, over all I found the plot fairly easy to follow (despite the fact that time travel usually just confuses the shit out of me). <br><br>- Building off of that, I loved the alternating perspectives of Marina and "Em." What's so interesting about it is that they are technically the same person and yet they are very different characters––since essentially they are the same girl but in different times/dimensions. Usually I'm not a fan of multiple first-person points of view––and you'd think in this case it would be even more confusing to tell the perspectives apart––but surprisingly I found it quite easy to differentiate the two voices from each other.<br><br>- The story really kept me guessing. It has a great balance of suspense and action, and I was constantly on the edge of my seat and wondering what on earth was going to happen. Although I <i>kind of</i> saw the ending coming, it wasn't until late in the book that I thought I knew how it was going to play out. For most of it, I had almost no idea what the conclusion would be.<br><br>- It was cool how there was not really a concrete "villain" in the story. Although James is sort of the antagonist, it's not completely black-and-white because we get to see two versions of him––both his innocent past self and his more sinister future self, and I found myself getting torn as to whether I should love him or hate him. And of course, Em is going through the same dilemma and the reader can really feel her struggle to decide what to do when she can't separate the James she grew up with from the James he turned out to be. <br><br>- In relation to my last point, I was impressed that the whole "evil villain plot" was quite original and actually kind of made sense. Of course, I use the term "evil villain" loosely because, as I said, I can't really bring myself to label James a "villain." But anyway, I was wondering how this whole time-travel thing was going to be used as a way to "endanger the whole world" and whatnot, and I was nervous it was going to be some totally half-assed and illogical explanation––but when I got to the explanation behind it I stopped and was like, "Wait … that's actually a pretty cool idea." (And I mean the author's idea to use as the explanation, not that the actual "evil plan" thing was a good idea.) Of course, I'm not going to give it away (except under the spoiler), but I can say that I found it to be quite intriguing.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[What I'm referring to is James's plan to use time-travel to set off a series of smaller threats/disasters in order to improve security to prevent bigger disasters––which of course would still mean hurting a lot of people and causing some kind of harshly regulated society, but in his mind it's justified because it means less people would die. Like, whoa. Just … whoa. That really blew my mind. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>- As I said in the beginning, I was surprised at how emotional this book became for me. I went into it having little-to-no expectation to become attached to the characters, but by the end I did really sympathize with them all. And when it came to the climax of the story, my heart was literally pounding and I was just so invested in it and worried about what would happen. Once again, I won't spoil anything without hiding it under a spoiler tag––but wow, the end is super intense in a lot of ways and bittersweet and I actually almost cried. <br><br>It was just so emotionally taxing that after I finished it, I literally lay down on the floor and rolled around. I'm not kidding.<br><br><b>
  <u>What didn't work for me:</u>
</b><br><br>- I did really like the ending, but I was also kind of confused about some things. After thinking about it for a while I basically figured it out, but it involved me actually sitting down and writing an explanation to myself about how the ending worked out. If anyone cares to read my (three) complicated explanation(s), here it is:<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><b>The simplified explanation:</b><br><br>Finn doesn't die because the version of James who kills him no longer exists. But I still don't understand why James #1 has to die; apparently it's because of some kind of paradox but I don't really get it.<br><br><b>The slightly more complicated version:</b><br><br>James #1: James who kills himself in the universe where Nate doesn't die<br>James #2: James who kills himself in the universe where Nate does die (in order to prevent himself from becoming evil future James)<br>James #3: Evil future James, who dies when #2 dies<br><br>Finn #1: Finn in the universe where James kills himself and Nate doesn't die<br>Finn #2: Finn in the universe where James #3 kills him<br>Finn #3: Future Finn, who dies when #2 dies<br><br>Marina #1: Marina in the universe where James kills himself and Nate doesn't die<br>Marina #2: Marina in the universe where Nate and Finn die<br>Marina #3: "Em," or future Marina who is trying to kill James, etc.<br><br><br>Basically, when James #2 kills himself, that causes James #3 to not exist anymore. Since James #3 is the one who kills Finn #2, that means that if James #3 no longer exists, then Finn #2 doesn't die. But James #2 is still dead, which is what creates the paradox that causes James #1 to die. And so, when James #2 kills himself, that erases Finn #2's death (because James #3, Finn #3, and Marina #3 no longer exist, since James is dead and Cassandra is never invented). Therefore, Finn #1 doesn't have to die because Finn #2 would not be dead; whereas, James #1 would have to be dead because James #2 would still be dead.<br><br><b>The even more rambly and complicated explanation:</b><br><br>Okay, so James 2 killed himself so that he would not turn into James 3. James 2 kills himself after he used to be James 1 (except in 2's universe, Nate dies). It's James 2's suicide that prevents him from becoming James 3, therefore preventing him from teaming up with Richter, therefore preventing Nate's death (which is why Nate doesn't die in 1's universe). So this creates a paradox because in 3's universe, Nate is still dead, and 3 is still the one who killed him. So there's a "ghost" of James that turns into James 3 and kills Nate; but now it's been changed so that Nate doesn't die and that never really happens.<br><br>But then, why does James 1 have to kill himself? If James 2's suicide created a paradox in which all three versions of James had to die, then why did Finn 2's death (which led to 3's death) not lead to Finn 1 dying? It could just be that James 1 killing himself is kind of an alternate universe/scenario and not really caused by James 2 killing himself in the future. But I guess it's also that if James 1 continued to exist, he would never become James 2 because Nate didn't die. And with Nate still alive, James 2 wouldn't have had the same drive to create Cassandra. So maybe James 1 had to kill himself because it would be impossible for him to live in a future without wanting to create Cassandra … ?<br><br>But also … if James 2 kills himself, then Cassandra is never invented––thus, not only would James 3 cease to exist, but also Finn 3 and Marina 3. (Although that's obvious I guess because the book pointed out multiple times that if James 2 or 3 died, Marina 3 and Finn 3 would cease to exist.) But if James 3 doesn't exist, then there is no one to kill Finn 2. So … I guess that's the answer? Finn 2 doesn't die in the future because James 3 doesn't exist to kill him … Therefore, he doesn't have to die in the past because he doesn't die in the future! Nailed it. I think. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>- The only thing I can think of that bothered me was pretty minor … It was just that I was kind of annoyed by the way female characters (besides Marina) were portrayed. Marina has a few female friends who––although they're extremely minor characters––are the pretty stereotypical "lol boys and make-up" type and don't seem to have any actual personalities. I know it's such a small thing, but … yeah. <br><br><b>The final word:</b><br><br>I went into this book with pretty low expectations, and I was glad that it surprised me in such a good way. I became very invested in the plot and characters, and this is one of the most original and compelling books I've read in the past year. <br><br>I was a bit nervous to find out there's going to be a sequel, since I thought this was very powerful as a standalone––so I hope things don't go downhill. But nevertheless, I highly recommend this book and I think Crisitin Terrill is a new author to look out for. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380378151i/733589.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>~ <a href="http://flyingkickapowreviews.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Flying Kick-a-pow! Reviews</a> ~</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17438987114068674867"><i>*4,5 stars*</i><br/><br/><i>I don't know how to start this review.</i><br/><br/>I could probably say that I regret not reading this book sooner. I could say that if you haven't read this book, you have to give it a chance. I could say that there were a lot of good things about this unique story that I loved, and I hope that you could love them too. The thing is, that <b>whatever I'm about to say, is never going to do this book justice. </b><br/><br/>I keep thinking about this story because it just blew my mind. <u>It blew it. </u><br/><br/>So I'll do my best </span>
  <span id="freeText17438987114068674867" style="display:none"><i>*4,5 stars*</i><br /><br /><i>I don't know how to start this review.</i><br /><br />I could probably say that I regret not reading this book sooner. I could say that if you haven't read this book, you have to give it a chance. I could say that there were a lot of good things about this unique story that I loved, and I hope that you could love them too. The thing is, that <b>whatever I'm about to say, is never going to do this book justice. </b><br /><br />I keep thinking about this story because it just blew my mind. <u>It blew it. </u><br /><br />So I'll do my best attempt to review this. (a.k.a just mumbling about how fantastic it actually was)<br /><br />I'm not gonna describe each character. I'll just say that this is a sci-fi novel about time-travels. More specific one time-travel mission about this two people who are trying to stop some terrible things to happen by destroying any possibility of the creation of time-travel machines in the first place. Because when this scientific, this "doctor" discovers the secret of time-traveling, the world goes to hell. And a lot of good people dies. So the best thing to try, is to stop this doctor to create it in the first place. Things get a lot difficult when these people travel in time. Because this book is narrated by two girls, one of the future and one of the past, and <b>in the past you would never EVER had imagine that the evil doctor from the future, is just a normal teenager</b>, with amazing friends. He's actually a good person. <br /><br />I loved that this book built this villain, and <b>we get to know him when he was just another normal boy</b>. And the way the two pov's in this book get intertwined is one of the best plot- twist I've ever read. Because at the beginning I didn't understand how those two girls were connected. And when I found out....WOW. Just WOW. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Finn and Em were my OTP. I loved how Finn was always in love with her, but it destroy me that she didn't notice because she was in love with James when they were kids. I'm happy that they get a future together, tho, James and Miranda were just not meant to be. And it leave me thinking a lot the fact that Em knows she has to kill James, and even after all the things he's done, she can't do it, because he was still her childhood best friend. Like, can you imagine? Knowing that someone you care about now, in the future will be an evil human-being? It must be terrible.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />All our yesterdays was a surprising book for me. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I didn't give it 5 stars because of the very ending. I was hoping for a more epic conclusion, also it leave sort of confused how Finn dies but not really??  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_681895849" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/681895849" />
    <a title="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller"><img alt="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517553177p2/13396599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/681895849?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" href="/user/show/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller">Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller?shelf=my-ya-library-catalogue">my-ya-library-catalogue</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer681895849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3713361805658885565">Via Book Reviews by Niki Hawkes at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.nikihawkes.com'>www.nikihawkes.com</a><br/><br/>[4.5 stars] All Our Yesterdays seems to garner mixed reactions from the amazing book bloggers I follow. Because it wasn’t getting across-the-board rave reviews, I decided to pass on it. I have to thank the marketing team at Netgalley for putting it back on my radar, because I absolutely loved it! It had me from the first page, and I set aside all my other books until I finished it (which is a rare thing for me, as I usually have about ten diff</span>
  <span id="freeText3713361805658885565" style="display:none">Via Book Reviews by Niki Hawkes at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.nikihawkes.com">www.nikihawkes.com</a><br /><br />[4.5 stars] All Our Yesterdays seems to garner mixed reactions from the amazing book bloggers I follow. Because it wasn’t getting across-the-board rave reviews, I decided to pass on it. I have to thank the marketing team at Netgalley for putting it back on my radar, because I absolutely loved it! It had me from the first page, and I set aside all my other books until I finished it (which is a rare thing for me, as I usually have about ten different books going at once).<br /><br />One of my favorite things about this novel (there was a few) is how well the story was organized. Everything unfolded almost effortlessly, yet I know it must’ve taken a ton of work. It flowed so well that I forgot to take notes for this post (which, with really awesome titles, I don’t need the notes anyway because I’m so fired up about them). In my eyes, it was brilliant.<br /><br />While the concept and world building were amazing, the real strength of this novel is in character development. Each character was distinct, vibrant, and written well enough to make me feel personally invested in their struggles. The range of dynamics she was able to get surrounding each individuals’ personality blew my mind. They were incredibly profound characters, and I guarantee I won’t be forgetting about them anytime soon.<br /><br />Time travel is difficult to do well – there always seems to be several frustrating plot holes. If there were inconsistencies in All Our Yesterdays, Terrill hid them well within her explanations of how time travel works. Her concepts mixed with the clear, beautiful writing has me convinced she is a truly brilliant author – you can tell this project took a lot of thought and planning. Even though I read this as a free digital copy, I liked it so much I bought the hardcover the day it came out. I will definitely be reading anything she publishes in the future!<br /><br />Recommended Reading: this book is fighting for a place in my top five favorite dystopians! Because of that, I plan on recommending it to fans of that genre – especially to those in the mood for something slightly different. Also to anyone wanting an atypical love story.<br /><br />Thank you NetGalley and Disney Book Group for the chance to read and review this title!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3713361805658885565" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_654377666" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/654377666" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/654377666?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781408835203" href="/book/show/18210450-all-our-yesterdays">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=alternating-povs">alternating-povs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=arc-2013">arc-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=best-of-2013">best-of-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=surprise-surprise">surprise-surprise</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=cover-lust">cover-lust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=open-ending">open-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2013">reviewed-in-2013</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer654377666" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7020955340524258122">All Our Yesterdays starts with one of the most impressive opening scenes I’ve come across in a very long time, possibly since Shatter Me. A drain in the floor seems like a very simple thing, but one that can become absolutely terrifying in the eyes of a prisoner. According to Cristin Terrill, it was this detail that prompted her to write the book in the first place, and it seems to have been an excellent place to start.<br/><br/>With that infamous drain in the very first sentence, getting pulled into Em’s</span>
  <span id="freeText7020955340524258122" style="display:none">All Our Yesterdays starts with one of the most impressive opening scenes I’ve come across in a very long time, possibly since Shatter Me. A drain in the floor seems like a very simple thing, but one that can become absolutely terrifying in the eyes of a prisoner. According to Cristin Terrill, it was this detail that prompted her to write the book in the first place, and it seems to have been an excellent place to start.<br><br>With that infamous drain in the very first sentence, getting pulled into Em’s and Marina’s respective stories proved to be almost effortless. Chapter after chapter, All Our Yesterdays is chock-full of action and tense moments. In addition, the two points of view from two-but-not-two narrators make this one of the most challenging and fascinating YA reads, narration-wise. If there’s one thing that needs to be said about Cristin Terrill, it’s that she used her excellent ideas to their full potential. <br><br>When it comes to time travel, I’m not ashamed to admit that I always struggle with the concept. All Our Yesterdays presented somewhat of a challenge in that regard, as I found it difficult to wrap my head around all those timelines, but I did enjoy trying. The psychological aspects of the story were equally interesting. Terrill explored the past and the present, the changes people go through and what they can and cannot influence. I don’t think there’s a person in this world who didn’t, at one point, wish to go back in time and shake some sense into their old self... or someone else, for that matter. <br><br>However, even with all the excitement and action (or precisely because of it), All Our Yesterdays failed to reach me emotionally. My feelings were those of admiration, enthusiasm and, more than once, outright fear, but to say that I was fully invested in the fate of these characters would be giving my relationship with the book far too much credit. When I remember how intensely I felt things when I was reading Unraveling by Elizabeth Norris, which is in many ways a similar book, All Our Yesterdays simply pales in comparison.<br><br>All grumpiness aside, please let me make this abundantly clear: All Our Yesterdays is a book you’ll definitely want to read. Terrill managed to bring something new to the table, and I don’t know about you, but thrill rides and romances are just about the only things that can hold my attention in this awful heat, and All Our Yesterday has more than enough of both.<br><br>This book is part of a duology, and although we still don’t have a release date for second book, I’m excited about it already. The first book wraps up nicely, but since that clearly isn't the end of things, I can't wait to see what is.<br><br><br><a href="http://www.thenocturnallibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226536i/681142.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="7020955340524258122" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1940989378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9355105753294960565">HOW DARE YOU. HOW DARE YOU. HOW DARE YOU. MEET ME IN THE PIT CRISTIN TERRIL. <br/><br/>Solid 5 stars and I'm currently crying. It's rare to find a book with a plot that's so exhilarating you can't stop reading. It's even rarer to find a book with well-crafted characters and well-built relationships. <b>This book had both.</b><br/><br/>This book is about... time travel? <i>All Our Yesterdays</i> opens with Em and Finn in a research studio, living in cells right next to each other, before they break out and pop into a time machine</span>
  <span id="freeText9355105753294960565" style="display:none">HOW DARE YOU. HOW DARE YOU. HOW DARE YOU. MEET ME IN THE PIT CRISTIN TERRIL. <br /><br />Solid 5 stars and I'm currently crying. It's rare to find a book with a plot that's so exhilarating you can't stop reading. It's even rarer to find a book with well-crafted characters and well-built relationships. <b>This book had both.</b><br /><br />This book is about... time travel? <i>All Our Yesterdays</i> opens with Em and Finn in a research studio, living in cells right next to each other, before they break out and pop into a time machine bound for a day four years ago. Don't read reviews of this book and get spoiled, because you WILL regret it. Cristin Terrill incorporates <b>so many twists and turns</b>, which I truly was not expecting. Just when you think you have everything figured out, there's a twist. Multiple times my expectations got flipped within a page. <br /><br />In terms of relationship building and character work, this book absolutely rocked. Em and Marina are complex, interesting narrators, and I grew to love them both. Em especially stands out; she's resourceful and clever, but so full of love and caring beneath the surface. Marina's character development was amazing, and I went from disliking her to feeling immense sympathy her. James is one of the most complex characters I've read about in a while, and needless to say, he broke my heart. <br /><br />You know how I have very few book ships and am very picky about romance? Terrill managed to make me love her couples anyway. Em and Finn were just... perfect. <b>They work so well together and are so honest with each other.</b> I want my relationship to be that healthy and loving. James and Marina broke my heart too, despite how much they bored me at the beginning. <br /><br />I basically only have one complaint, and that is the first 100 pages. Em's opening moments are awesome, but Marina's chapters are superficial and annoying. Trust me, that goes away with a bang; a twist that left me desperate to keep reading. <br /><br />Not only did this book manage to make me fall in love with its characters, it also was a major mindfuck. Seriously, this book is plotted crazily well. And that ending was pitch-perfect in every way. Recommended to everyone under the sun. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9355105753294960565" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1089671054?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408835197" href="/book/show/17451105-all-our-yesterdays">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=likeable-mc">likeable-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=alternative-pov">alternative-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-ya-and-fantasy">fave-ya-and-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=knots-in-my-stomach">knots-in-my-stomach</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-characters">fave-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=romance-i-root-for">romance-i-root-for</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=made-me-laugh">made-me-laugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1089671054" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2636470203110776970"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1460294653i/18723326._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>"James leans against the wall, letting it takes his weight. "You two <i>agree</i> on this?"<br/>" I know, it's weird," Finn says. "I feel dirty."</b>
</blockquote><br/><b><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13514612.All_Our_Yesterdays' title='All Our Yesterdays by Cristin Terrill' rel='nofollow noopener'>All Our Yesterdays</a> has been lingering in my mind for almost 2 years now</b>. That's why it deserved a real review, even if talking about the plot is pretty challenging without spoiling anything. I tried my best, okay?<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1460294653i/18723327._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Let's talk about the <b>plot</b>....<br/><br/>... without <i>really</i> talking about the plot?? <br/><br/>(yes, I can do this?)<br/><br/>*sharp intake of breath*<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13514612.All_Our_Yesterdays' title='All Our Yesterdays by Cristin Terrill' rel='nofollow noopener'>All Our Yesterdays</a> brings us <b>in </b></span>
  <span id="freeText2636470203110776970" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1460294653i/18723326._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"James leans against the wall, letting it takes his weight. "You two <i>agree</i> on this?"<br>" I know, it's weird," Finn says. "I feel dirty."</b>
</blockquote><br><b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13514612.All_Our_Yesterdays" title="All Our Yesterdays by Cristin Terrill" rel="nofollow noopener">All Our Yesterdays</a> has been lingering in my mind for almost 2 years now</b>. That's why it deserved a real review, even if talking about the plot is pretty challenging without spoiling anything. I tried my best, okay?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1460294653i/18723327._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Let's talk about the <b>plot</b>....<br><br>... without <i>really</i> talking about the plot?? <br><br>(yes, I can do this?)<br><br>*sharp intake of breath*<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13514612.All_Our_Yesterdays" title="All Our Yesterdays by Cristin Terrill" rel="nofollow noopener">All Our Yesterdays</a> brings us <b>in a shattered world where time travel is not only a reality, but also a oh so frightening weapon</b> when hold by delusional and powerful hands. <br><br>Time travel, REALLY? Okay. I must admit that while I often like time-travel stories <s>except when they involve old Scottish marriage rules because really, what the fuck</s> I usually spend a great time suspending my disbelief something fierce - <i>of course</i> I know that I'm reading a science-fiction book, hey, I'm not a fool but I <b>need</b> to be able to rely on <i>some</i> believable explanations <i>or</i> I'm not buying it. <br><br>I mean, lazy much? <br><br>So, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13514612.All_Our_Yesterdays" title="All Our Yesterdays by Cristin Terrill" rel="nofollow noopener">All Our Yesterdays</a>? I have to congratulate <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5767141.Cristin_Terrill" title="Cristin Terrill" rel="nofollow noopener">Cristin Terrill</a> because I find myself accepting and <i>believing</i> the explanations The Doctor gives us - The Doctor <i>aka</i> The Evil, and no, I won't say anything else about him, except he's the creator and user of the time machine, Cassandra (I can't be the only one noticing a messed-up joke in <i>that</i> name?? <i>Cassandre? Reaaally?</i>) <br><br><u>Verdict</u> : I finished that book with the *almost* absolute certainty that it could be possible to create such a dreading machine - and what a scaring possibility, I'm telling you! <br><br>About the ending : <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[this is REAL spoiler, open at your own risk<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I know that some readers were annoyed by it, but it made sense to me at the time. If I remember correctly, I think what I understood is this : as the version of James who killed Finn doesn't exist anymore, Finn didn't die. I think? There was more, but I can't remember? Sorry? It involves a lot of James#1, James#2, James#3, and honestly, it took me a long thinking AT THE TIME to get it, so 2 years after? Well... I cannot explain??? I'm sorry? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1460294653i/18723328._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There's no denying that I <b>loved</b> these characters. WHY? <br><br>That's pretty simple actually : <b>they're so realistic I could almost grasp them</b>. Throughout the story we witness their evolution and I enjoyed their growth <i>a lot</i> : Call me cynical, but I never believed in this bad guys/good guys dichotomy. Indeed I think that sometimes people drive on a thin ice without knowing it, and as we say in French, <i>l'enfer est pavé de bonnes intentions</i>, understand : even if we think we're doing the <i>right</i> thing, unexpected really <i>bad</i> things can arise from our so-called <i>good</i> actions. <br><br>We're in real life here, and from a sci-fi novel, I say <i>bravo</i>. Both <b>Em</b> or <b>Finn</b> grow fiercer and fiercer, all the events and suffering they have to go through making their final resolution completely believable and understandable. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"I glance at Finn to see if he's starting to sweat and shake the way I am, but he seems unaffected. He's probably been working out in his cell, the vain little bastard."</b>
</blockquote><br><b>How can we recognize a good characterization?</b> <br>Huuuum, <u>Let's see</u> : <br><br>☛ <b>Option 1</b> <br>Character A is character A at the beginning of the story.<br>Character A is put in the middle of a war-a wild and frightening world-<i>whatever, OKAY?</i><br>Character A never changes and stays Character A in the end of the story.<br><b><u>Character A is a robot</u>. He bores me to no end. I want him to die or to come back in his little village (you <i>know</i> who I mean, don't you?)</b><br><br>☛ <b>Option 2</b> <br>Character A is character A at the beginning of the story.<br>Character A is put in the middle of a war-a wild and frightening world-<i>whatever, OKAY?</i><br>Character A evolves through the story and becomes Character <i>A'</i>.<br><b><u>Character <i>A'</i> is believable</u>. I love Character <i>A'</i>.</b><br><br>As you can guess, in my opinion <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13514612.All_Our_Yesterdays" title="All Our Yesterdays by Cristin Terrill" rel="nofollow noopener">All Our Yesterdays</a> belongs to the second option. <i>Plus</i>, icing on the cake, I loved <b>Finn</b>'s character from beginning to the end, from the sarcastic and loyal best-friend to the adorable and fierce cell-mate. <br><br>Saving the world is not easy, but if I had to choose a teammate, Finn would seem a really great option. Trust me. <br><br><b>To sum-up, what do we have here?</b><br><br>- A <b>compelling, fascinating and fast-paced plot</b> served by a never boring writing enlightened with sparks of humor. <br><br>- The underlying issue of the <b>natural attraction humans feel for Power</b> and the changes it can lead to.<br><br>- <b>Flawed, believable and fierce characters</b> including a heart-warming and funny male-lead. <br><br> <b>Convinced?</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"But maybe it's simpler than that. Maybe it's that Finn has this magical ability to make you smile even when things are grim."</b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1460244805i/18718125._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_669492257" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/669492257" />
    <a title="Brandi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4765786-brandi"><img alt="Brandi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1431565587p2/4765786.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/669492257?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandi" href="/user/show/4765786-brandi">Brandi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone!</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Brandi by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4765786-brandi?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer669492257" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6476602807019372634"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <br/>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>""You have to kill him." Imprisoned in the heart of a secret military base, Em has nothing except the voice of the boy in the cell next door and the list of instructions she finds taped inside the drain.<br/><br/>Marina has loved her best friend James since the day he moved next door when they were children. A gorgeous, introverted science prodigy from one of America’s most famous families, James finally seems to be seeing Marina in a new way, too. But on one disastrous night, James’s life crumbles</b></span>
  <span id="freeText6476602807019372634" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>""You have to kill him." Imprisoned in the heart of a secret military base, Em has nothing except the voice of the boy in the cell next door and the list of instructions she finds taped inside the drain.<br><br>Marina has loved her best friend James since the day he moved next door when they were children. A gorgeous, introverted science prodigy from one of America’s most famous families, James finally seems to be seeing Marina in a new way, too. But on one disastrous night, James’s life crumbles apart, and with it, Marina’s hopes for their future. Now someone is trying to kill him. Marina will protect James, no matter what. Even if it means opening her eyes to a truth so terrible that she may not survive it. At least not as the girl she once was."</b><br><br>I think that the synopsis is perfect and have nothing to add to it, which is why I've decided to use it in my review. I <i>loved</i> this book! The writing is wonderful; full of tension, some mystery, angst, humor, and pain. I wasn't even five chapters into the story before I could tell it would be a book that I'd love; it didn't have to grow on me or require me to be forgiving to enjoy it. I plan on reading whatever <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5767141.Cristin_Terrill" title="Cristin Terrill" rel="nofollow noopener">Cristin Terrill</a> puts out next, because she knows how to write a spectacular character driven story!!<br><br>It didn't take long to realize who the Doctor was that Em is so afraid of, but it did take me a minute to realize who <i>Em</i> was, lol. It isn't a secret that Em is going back in time to stop the creation of that time machine (it's the only one in the world as far as we know), and what I thought were two characters are actually just one. This was so horrible to experience with Em because really, what would you do to protect a younger version of yourself from such horrible events?! I teared up a few times while reading this late into the night, and though the ending was slightly too perfect for my tastes, I still wish it had been longer just so that I didn't have to let go. <br><br>Finn is on my list as one of my favorite males, and he kind of reminded me of Roar, though less platonic, lol. Marina was wonderfully realistic, and it was interesting to see how she and Em compared to each other. James...James is harder for me. On one hand I really liked his shy nerdiness, and on the other I found his evolution to be <i>slightly</i> hard to believe. Not that I didn't believe almost all of what he became, but the part where he keeps insisting that Em 'betrayed' him, referred to the paper she had as 'documents' <s>that I didn't understand why he would need considering he completed his research</s>, and what he was doing during the climax of the story...was a little much I guess. Not bad, just a little much. <br><br>If you're like me and a well written character driven story is what makes you happiest, then I can't recommend this book highly enough for you! If you like a wonderfully tense and layered plot that keeps you on the edge of your seat, then I can't recommend this book highly enough for you! If you just like <b>good</b> stories, then--well you get the idea. <br><br>Read this.<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="6476602807019372634" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1319319661?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" href="/user/show/7366569-fafa-s-book-corner">Fafa&#39;s Book Corner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1319319661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6013287417292451869">**Warning: this text may contain spoilers** This is my first time travel book. I used to avoid them because I thought that it would become to confusing for me to understand. But after hearing about this and knowing the basic plot line I decided to give it a shot. Let me tell you I don't regret it. I have never read something so complicated but absolutely brilliant at the same time. The world building in this book was told to us by Em. Even though it was told to us you can see that the author put</span>
  <span id="freeText6013287417292451869" style="display:none">**Warning: this text may contain spoilers** This is my first time travel book. I used to avoid them because I thought that it would become to confusing for me to understand. But after hearing about this and knowing the basic plot line I decided to give it a shot. Let me tell you I don't regret it. I have never read something so complicated but absolutely brilliant at the same time. The world building in this book was told to us by Em. Even though it was told to us you can see that the author put quite a bit of work into this. I don't think I have ever read about such a complicated world. In a way this novel is a dystopia. As well as Sci-Fi. I think there are a lot of lessons to be taken from this book. For example with James. At eighteen years he was sweet and innocent but as the doctor he was insane and corrupt. I think specifically what you can take from is while you have your dreams and desires you have to make sure that doesn't consume you the way it did the doctor with Cassandra. He became so obsessed with 'doing good' that he lost himself along the way. From Marina you can learn that you do in fact have loved ones and you do have a right to love yourself. And lastly from Finn you can learn to sacrifice your own happiness to make others happy. And when make others happy put a smile on your face and make some pretty funny jokes. I recommend this to everyone!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6013287417292451869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_638830764" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/638830764" />
    <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata"><img alt="Faye, la Patata" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557835753p2/7650833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/638830764?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faye, la Patata" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata">Faye, la Patata</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=best-books-i-ve-ever-read">best-books-i-ve-ever-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=multiple-povs">multiple-povs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=good-hero">good-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=good-heroine">good-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer638830764" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15602676530500418670"><a href='http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net/2013/07/16/review-all-our-yesterdays-by-cristin-terrill/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <b>Hey, PH readers! Want to win an ARC of All Our Yesterdays? And to the rest of you, want a finished copy of the book? Join my giveaways now! Head on over the blog to get a chance to win!</b>
</a><br/><br/><a href='http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380238998i/681660._SX540_.png' height='120' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Wow. That was one fantastic ride.<br/><br/>Just so everyone knows, I love Time Travel stories. This adoration started after I read Jude Deveraux's <em>A Knight in Shining</em> <em>Armor</em>, where a young woman finds a man from the 1500s transported in her time and she to his later.<em> </em>The idea of changing the future by going back to t</span>
  <span id="freeText15602676530500418670" style="display:none"><a href="http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net/2013/07/16/review-all-our-yesterdays-by-cristin-terrill/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Hey, PH readers! Want to win an ARC of All Our Yesterdays? And to the rest of you, want a finished copy of the book? Join my giveaways now! Head on over the blog to get a chance to win!</b>
</a><br><br><a href="http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380238998i/681660._SX540_.png" height="120" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Wow. That was one fantastic ride.<br><br>Just so everyone knows, I love Time Travel stories. This adoration started after I read Jude Deveraux's <em>A Knight in Shining</em> <em>Armor</em>, where a young woman finds a man from the 1500s transported in her time and she to his later.<em> </em>The idea of changing the future by going back to the past was just excitingly intriguing to me, and I've been on a hunt ever since for books with the same concept and quality. Unfortunately, the ones I've found were very disappointing, and I was beginning to think I wouldn't be able to find a book as good as Deveraux's. Then came <em>All Our Yesterdays. </em>And right now, all I'm thinking is, <strong>
  <em>WHERE HAVE YOU BEEN ALL MY LIFE?!?!</em>
</strong><br><br>This book is seriously mind-fucking good. I don't even know where to start.<br><br><strong>I loved how it has that sense of urgency, that feeling where if we don't read fast enough, we'll run out of time, that everything will end, and our two characters' efforts will be for naught. </strong>Into the future, we see the tale unfold in Em's eyes, as she and Finn must go back to the past to make things right, and the only way to make it right is to kill <em>him.</em> This proves to be quite difficult, however, as they find themselves running against time, especially since the sight of their younger, inexperienced selves make the task even harder.<br><br><strong>The plot is incredibly fast-paced, and kept me on my toes every single page, my heart pounding, my throat tightening, as I anticipated what was going to come next. </strong>I kid you not when I say there was never a dull moment in this book. And you know the best part is? THEY EXPLAINED VERY WELL THE SCIENCE STUFF! We all know the paradoxes that can result from time travel, but it was explained here very well how time is not exactly linear, and that there are forces that avoid such things from happening. So those loopholes that I've found? Poof! Right out of the window. You can really tell the plot and world-building were well thought-out and I absolutely appreciated that, especially since I'm quite cynical.<br><br><strong><strong>But the strongest factor of this book is neither the plot nor the world-building. What made <em>All Our Yesterdays</em> spectacular were the characters -</strong> <b>Em, Marina, the two Finns, and even James.</b> <strong>They were so three-dimensional and well-rounded that I couldn't help but imagine they were real people, and that made me feel so much for them</strong>. </strong>Em is absolutely kick-ass – she knows what she needs to do and understands the gravity of their situation, but even though her heart has hardened and her resolve like stone, she still has gentleness within her that makes her hesitant into becoming a killer. Many times she had the opportunity to kill the one she had come to kill, a person who was very dear to her in the past, but in these same instances we see her reluctance, her resolve unwavering at the sight of their younger, innocent selves.<br><br><strong>And Marina? Even though she did questionable decisions and was whiny, insensitive, and mean sometimes, I got to love her, anyway. She was insecure and badly in love that her actions were merely because in her heart, she believed she was doing the right thing.</strong> The intentions were all there, and even though some of what she did were not exactly the best things to do, you know that she's got heart, anyway. It was so heartrending  to see this bubbly sixteen year old and then Em, so hardened with the miserable experience she had and what Marina will endure as well if they don't change things. It's the contrast of the <em>before</em> and <em>after</em> that got to me, and made me understand how much  the future Marina wanted to protect the younger one as much as she possibly could.<br><br><strong></strong><strong>This book also has one of the most bittersweet endings I've ever read</strong>. I don't want to spoil it (even though throughout reading it, I've restrained myself greatly from taking a sneak peek of the last page just to see if things will be alright in the end) as it will take the magic away, but it seriously made me tear up. <strong>On the outside, it may not really look that powerful, but the context of the whole novel and the understanding we get from the future selves made its impact just so emotional and equally thought-provoking. </strong><br><br>Overall, I'm excited for the rest of the world to read this. This novel is more than just a sci-fi thriller. It has values as well, and reminds us that technology is a double-edged sword, and that too much power can even blind people with good-intentions. More importantly, this book also calls everyone to love and respect ourselves more, to be strong and confident, to be humble. This is a stunning debut, and Hyperion hit the nail on the head with this one.<br><br><strong>Final Verdict: 4.5 / 5 stars!</strong><br><br><em>An ARC was provided by the publisher in exchange for a review. This did not influence my thoughts in any way.</em></span>
  <a data-text-id="15602676530500418670" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_626949584" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/626949584" />
    <a title="Jasprit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4841793-jasprit"><img alt="Jasprit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456315622p2/4841793.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/626949584?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasprit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasprit" href="/user/show/4841793-jasprit">Jasprit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781408835203" href="/book/show/18210450-all-our-yesterdays">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=out-2013">out-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=arc-galley">arc-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer626949584" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11720797454268588387">Wow this book was utterly amazing. I know I’ve read some great reads this year, but All Our Yesterdays will definitely stand out from among the rest for a long time to come. What I loved most about this book was that I hardly knew anything about it before going into it. I read the blurb ages ago and was totally excited, but when I started reading I was utterly amazed and surprised with what Terrill had planned for us.<br/><br/>The basic crux of the story is time travel, two characters Em and Finn are dedi</span>
  <span id="freeText11720797454268588387" style="display:none">Wow this book was utterly amazing. I know I’ve read some great reads this year, but All Our Yesterdays will definitely stand out from among the rest for a long time to come. What I loved most about this book was that I hardly knew anything about it before going into it. I read the blurb ages ago and was totally excited, but when I started reading I was utterly amazed and surprised with what Terrill had planned for us.<br /><br />The basic crux of the story is time travel, two characters Em and Finn are dedicated to changing the future, it’s crucial they do this, as all the future entails for them is torture, and heartache, it is pretty much a bleak future no one would ever wish upon. At first I had no clue as why Finn and Em were hell bent on changing the past, we were given a brief snippet into what they had to deal with, but as the story progressed we got to learn the horrible truth I was so surprised but also a little bit hurt. Because the story alternates with flashbacks to what’s happened in the future and what’s happened in the past, I found it so hard to comprehend just how significantly a character could change. We were shown painstakingly obvious evidence right in front of our eyes, but maybe because I didn’t want to accept that this particular character in the past and in the future could be the same person. It kind of broke my heart, as I actually started this book with this character being my favourite. They did have a lot to deal with and so I could fully understand their slowly changing behaviour. But they were so lost I just wanted to hug them. And then I felt even more wretched for feeling sorry for them when I was given snippets of their tender and caring side after everything Em and Finn had been through. Seriously Terrill sure knows how to trample all over your heart.<br /><br />Finn and Em were amazing characters, I adore the insecure and under confident Em in the past and the tough and still torn Em of the future. She reminded me a bit of Tris from the Divergent series, she was at first always unsure about herself, but she proved herself to be one fearless and clever character. I loved the banter between her character and Finn, and just their entire relationship; it had changed so significantly that I was just glad they were constantly there for one another.<br /><br />The entire concept that Terrill created was just so unique in my eyes. I’m not typically a person who reads time travel books, but Terrill’s immense world building and gorgeous writing lured me in from the very first page. (You should have seen my kindle it was full with highlights of passages which ripped my heart). Terrill has also the knack of creating characters that you never want to let go, the characters in this book were fresh, charismatic and always bringing something different. I adored watching their friendships develop and how each character tried to deal with so much inner turmoil along the way.<br /><br />All Our Yesterdays was a wonderfully executed debut, it had everything I love reading about; flawless characters which show exceptional growth, a scary but totally realistic world, non- stop action, a story which kept me on my toes with me having no idea which way things could end and of course a nice pinch of heartache. But it also had many things which make me eager to jump into books of a similar genre. Terrill has weaved a beautiful story in All Our Yesterdays and for that I encourage you all to pick it up.<br /><br />This review can be found on <a href="http://www.thereadersden.blogspot.co.uk/2013/07/review-all-our-yesterdays-by-cristin.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readers Den</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11720797454268588387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1113649365" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1113649365" />
    <a title="Rachel E. Carter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29482005-rachel-e-carter"><img alt="Rachel E. Carter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512593159p2/29482005.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1113649365?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel E. Carter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel E. Carter" href="/user/show/29482005-rachel-e-carter">Rachel E. Carter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29482005-rachel-e-carter?shelf=have-paperback">have-paperback</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1113649365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18127252979342071857"><b>"There's always hope for us..."</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417318755ra/12292955.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Love, love, love that this was a standalone. The beginning was so dramatic which pulled me in right away (reminded me of the beginning of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10429045.Shatter_Me__Shatter_Me___1_' title='Shatter Me (Shatter Me, #1) by Tahereh Mafi' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shatter Me</a>, I don't know why, I just love prison/dungeon scenes), and while a lot of things were predictable, the book was still a worthwhile read & really no boring parts. Loved Fin & Em and even, in some ways, James. I thought the action was perfect and the funeral scene at the end was great with the flashbacks with Fin & James</span>
  <span id="freeText18127252979342071857" style="display:none"><b>"There's always hope for us..."</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417318755ra/12292955.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Love, love, love that this was a standalone. The beginning was so dramatic which pulled me in right away (reminded me of the beginning of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10429045.Shatter_Me__Shatter_Me___1_" title="Shatter Me (Shatter Me, #1) by Tahereh Mafi" rel="nofollow noopener">Shatter Me</a>, I don't know why, I just love prison/dungeon scenes), and while a lot of things were predictable, the book was still a worthwhile read &amp; really no boring parts. Loved Fin &amp; Em and even, in some ways, James. I thought the action was perfect and the funeral scene at the end was great with the flashbacks with Fin &amp; James (it made me cry twice!). <br><br>My only complaints are: 1) We never got to see the actual scene when Marina changed her name. I felt like it was never explained how she decided on "Em." Even a sentence would have been helpful, like: "My middle name is Emily." Maybe I missed this? 2) I wish I had seen a bit more into how Fin &amp; Em fell in love on the run or even as Fin &amp; Marina. Yes, I know that we know what will happen for them, but I felt like I wasn't as fully invested in them as I could have been in the two as a couple because I only got Fin/Em already-in-love and Fin/Marina friends-kind-of. Yes, there were small hints at more and that kiss scene while they were on the run but it just was missing a bit for me -like, how, in reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1656001.The_Host__The_Host___1_" title="The Host (The Host, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">The Host</a> I was never fully invested in Jared/Mel because the flashbacks were minimal, I was rooting for Wanderer/Ian because I got to see their relationship develop &amp; that is always my favorite part. <br><br>That said, All Our Yesterdays really was amazing and even though I wanted a bit more of Fin/Marina, the author stayed true to her vision &amp; everything she did made perfect sense, it's just a matter of preference for me. Still, I will definitely read her future books -this was a great book &amp; I had so much fun reading it &lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="18127252979342071857" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
