<div id="review_688546597" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/688546597" />
    <a title="Mitch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8170554-mitch"><img alt="Mitch" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396208595p2/8170554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/688546597?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mitch" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mitch" href="/user/show/8170554-mitch">Mitch</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781408835203" href="/book/show/18210450-all-our-yesterdays">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer688546597" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10301626342664019952"><u>All Our Yesterdays</u> is I think the first book I've enjoyed <i>despite</i> the premise. I know that may sound like an odd thing to say, and maybe it's just me, but when I read the summary I really thought I was being promised a complex, mind-bending time travel plot. I mean, a girl travels back in time to stop a madman - that has <u>Terminator</u> written all over it, doesn't it? - but instead how Cristin Terrill handled the time travel made <i>me</i> want to travel back in time and erase the fact that I've read this.</span>
  <span id="freeText10301626342664019952" style="display:none"><u>All Our Yesterdays</u> is I think the first book I've enjoyed <i>despite</i> the premise. I know that may sound like an odd thing to say, and maybe it's just me, but when I read the summary I really thought I was being promised a complex, mind-bending time travel plot. I mean, a girl travels back in time to stop a madman - that has <u>Terminator</u> written all over it, doesn't it? - but instead how Cristin Terrill handled the time travel made <i>me</i> want to travel back in time and erase the fact that I've read this. Still, I'm <s>an honest guy</s> ok so I'm a pathological liar - but I would never lie about how I feel about a book, integrity and all - so I have to admit even though the time travel didn't work for me, I still liked the parts of the book that happen in the present, because those chapters at least worked by reading like a pretty decent political thriller.<br /><br />Here's my problem with the time travel: the alternating chapters between the future character (Em) and the present character (Marina) don't really mesh at first, and when Terrill finally gets them together at the same time (not a pun), she seems to do everything in her power to <i>avoid</i> time paradoxes. In other words, we have two chapters with Em in prison in the future, a few chapters of Marina being a shallow DC socialite in the present, then a chapter of Em escaping in the future - rather than feeling like a single cohesive narrative, it's like reading two completely unrelated plots that only barely come together at the end. For a book about time travel, it's just so poorly done; my guess is Terrill is still thinking in linear time, so the time travel ends up being a rather weak gimmick rather than a fully integrated part of the plot, you know where things that are happening butterfly effect out to affect things that happened earlier in the book, the way time travel is supposed to be done. In fact, I'm not kidding when I say Terrill goes out of her way to avoid time paradoxes - one of the first rules she lays down about time travel is that time is sentient and takes care of the paradoxes on its own, and I'm sorry but WTF that's like saying length or width is intelligent and my desk drawer will organize itself because those dimensions will know when something is out of place. I don't know if it's a good thing then that time travel only comes into play twice, once with how Em escapes at the beginning basically recycling a fairly common time travel trope involving causal loops, and once at the end resolving the whole thing with yet another nonsensical time travel rule <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[a moment in time can be 'fixed' because a 'remnant' of the traveler stays behind to make sure the event happens and just no, what a cop out <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Yeah I'm disappointed, a well done time paradox for me <i>makes</i> a time travel book, even in <u>Terminator</u> we have a time paradox with Skynet basically causing John Conner to be born by sending the Terminator back in time to kill him, and Terrill's approach in comparison is just lazy.<br /><br />With that rant on time travel out of the way, I do have a few things to say about the characters. First, apparently (spoiler alert) it's not supposed to be entirely obvious whether Em is a future version of Marina, but I don't see anyone who's confused about that and considering Finn calls her M... yeah, it felt to me like Terrill wanted to leave some ambiguity about it but kept forgetting as she was writing and the end result is Em's relationship to Marina seems so wishy-washy. As for Marina herself, I don't think I need to say more than this quote from the author:<br /><blockquote><br />Don't worry so much about making Marina likable in the beginning. She's a rich bitch with a heart of gold; embrace that. Once you do, she'll come to life for you.<br /></blockquote><br />Definitely embraced alright. Then again, it's hard for me to see how the characters grow from their present selves into their future selves, Marina's about as superficial at the end as she is throughout the entire story, and I don't think enough's done to make James feel like he could grow into a threat in four years time, so while the idea of stopping a monster was intriguing, I didn't get the sense of James <i>being</i> that monster required to really make it work; it was almost like they were killing a completely separate person. As for Em, she doesn't do much besides angst over whether to shoot James for much of the book and I found her storyline so much weaker than Marina's and constantly wished I could be past her chapters so I could see how Marina's much more interesting storyline was playing out - oh, and how stupid can she be to think <i>looking</i> at her past self will destroy the universe? That's not how physics works.<br /><br />Ok, I know I'm being a downer, considering I did like this book after all, so here's the part where I assure you the raving reviews all have merit. Terrill's writing is fast paced and being a DC kid myself I love how the story when it's not about time travel - most of the book actually - reads like a young adult political thriller, sort of like a cross between <u>Gossip Girl</u> and <u>24</u>, but definitely way better than the images that comparison may conjure up. There's a pretty intense side plot involving an assassination attempt against James's brother Nate, and despite how the time travel is the talk of the town here, for me it was actually the government conspiracy stuff that saved <u>All Our Yesterdays</u> from being a total dud. I liked seeing James and Marina trying to get to the bottom of it, watching Terrill develop James's character in relation to his whole political family, and it's all pretty easy to appreciate because Terrill keeps the conspiracy stuff compartmentalized and distinct from though tangentially related to the time travel stuff, but then the time travel has to rear its ugly head almost like a marginally logical twist that I knew was coming and even with all the heart put into James and Finn I just can't reconcile the parts of the book that involved time travel with the parts that didn't, what was an interesting and intriguing story just fell prey to a climax and ending of manipulation and convenience - I really think it says something when I feel the beginning, Em's chapters, and the ending are the weakest parts of the book.<br /><br />Basically - <u>All Our Yesterdays</u> is a neat thriller, but doesn't work nearly so well with time travel thrown in. Although, if Cristin Terrill were ever to write a political thriller, just a political thriller, I would totally be on board (hint hint).</span>
  <a data-text-id="10301626342664019952" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_898146158" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/898146158" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/898146158?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=awesome-heroines">awesome-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=my-favorite-covers">my-favorite-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=alternating-pov">alternating-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=tearjerkers">tearjerkers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=white-knuckle-cliffies">white-knuckle-cliffies</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer898146158" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10526125607632232142">I hated this. No, wait, I loved this. No, no-<b>I hated it....Right?</b> Still, even after having finished a day and a half ago, I still don't know what I think of this book. It played with my heart on the deepest emotional level possible...and, for once, I don't know if that was a good thing. <br/><br/>Dealing with matters of the heart are messy. There is no way to make rational decisions when your heart is split down the middle-I believe that with my whole soul. And, believe it or not, I'm not even talking abo</span>
  <span id="freeText10526125607632232142" style="display:none">I hated this. No, wait, I loved this. No, no-<b>I hated it....Right?</b> Still, even after having finished a day and a half ago, I still don't know what I think of this book. It played with my heart on the deepest emotional level possible...and, for once, I don't know if that was a good thing. <br><br>Dealing with matters of the heart are messy. There is no way to make rational decisions when your heart is split down the middle-I believe that with my whole soul. And, believe it or not, I'm not even talking about a love triangle. This is a good old-fashioned torture of the heart, a total mind-fuck...and I'm not sure I handled it all that well. <br><br>When I picked up this book, I thought I was starting a run of the mill dystopian/sci-fi fantasy novel. Honest to God, I might have rethought my decision to start this had I known how it would rip my heart into shreds. I keep telling my friends all the events of the book and we all came to the same type of stuttery, open-mouthed, grappling for words conclusion-<b>Even after countless reviews and a neurotic fetish with making sure it fit all my criteria (I do this for every book I'm about to read, lest I make bad decisions), I still wasn't prepared for what this book was truly about.</b> If you simply read the blurb, you see it's about two different couples in two different times, so to speak. You realize it's all about time travel and deciding what you would change if you could: Are you <i>really</i> fixing something if you go back in time and alter the past? But what that damn dirty blurb doesn't tell you is this-<b>This book is far deeper than even it's author lets on. This book has such raw, magnetic moments that you can't help but to be manipulated by each individual character and each individual motivation. This book is so multi-layered that you won't know what side you're on, who you're rooting for, or who you <i>should</i> be rooting for. </b> The simple truth is this: there is no good or evil, it is simply what your present self knows the future to be. It's what you're willing to do, what you're <b>willing to sacrifice</b> to make the world a better place-even if it destroys you to have to do so.<br><br>Im sorry, but this story? It's characters? Their struggles ? They killed me. Each moment killed me. And in the end, no matter what needed to happen...I still don't know If I'll ever fully get over it. <br><br>I loved the characters, all of them, and I think that's why I was so heartbroken at each and every turn. This book was everything I've come to love as I've progressed as a reader...and maybe it was so PERFECTLY DONE that I wasn't ready for it. Maybe it was so <b>perfectly fucked up</b> and so twisted that I literally was kicked in the chest, blind-sided by the brilliance that was this beautiful piece of a fucked up world. <br><br>It doesn't make sense, and I guess it doesn't have to. <b>I, the girl who named herself after the peril she so desperately seeks, <i>could. Not. Handle. The. Peril.</i></b> Emotionally or otherwise. It tore me to shreds. It knocked me on my ass. And, in the end, I was a blubbering mess curled up in a ball who wanted a better end for these best friends who never had a fucking chance. Not all of them, at least. <br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/crushing-my-heart_zpsbeca2230.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409062370ra/10928492.gif" alt=" photo crushing-my-heart_zpsbeca2230.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Read it. Don't read it. I don't care-I am a mess. The vulnerability, the love, the sacrifice-God I loved that...but after it's all over...my heart couldn't handle it. Maybe another time, another place. If only I could use that damn time machine to transport back a couple days and slap myself in the face so I would be more prepared...Hmm. Oh well. <b>Check-Mate, Motherfucker.</b> Chelsea loses.<br><br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491628712i/22430034._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>

<div id="review_1198794666" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1198794666" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4844873-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1299680097p2/4844873.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1198794666?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/4844873-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Laura by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4844873-laura?shelf=falling-for-the-boy-next-door">falling-for-the-boy-next-door</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1198794666" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11243671498296241297"><br/><b>Time is coming for us, and coming fast. </b><br/><br/>Time takes and gives so much. We age, change, hurt and love. Over time, we can lose ourselves. Lose sight of what we wanted to do or be in life. If you had the chance to look back four or five years, would you recognize yourself? What has time done to you? Would you shake your head and giggle or cringe at your decisions? I look back and see someone so open. I want to reach across time and yell, warn her to protect her heart. But what would that change? Who</span>
  <span id="freeText11243671498296241297" style="display:none"><br /><b>Time is coming for us, and coming fast. </b><br /><br />Time takes and gives so much. We age, change, hurt and love. Over time, we can lose ourselves. Lose sight of what we wanted to do or be in life. If you had the chance to look back four or five years, would you recognize yourself? What has time done to you? Would you shake your head and giggle or cringe at your decisions? I look back and see someone so open. I want to reach across time and yell, warn her to protect her heart. But what would that change? Who would I be without the love I had and lost? Who would I be now?<br /><br />All Our Yesterdays by Cristin Terrill tells a story of time, time travel, friendship, and love. Marina has been in love with her best friend and boy next door for years. James, the genius boy next door, is just beginning to make Marina believe they could have a future together as more than friends when tragedy strikes. Everything changes in a flash. From friendship to family to love! Anything and everything can change in an instant. Friends—James, Finn, Em, and Marina—learn that again and again in this time traveling, suspense filled ride! I loved these four characters. The way they argued, flirted, and laughed. Tension, banter and mystery all stirred together. They made me smile, think, and “aww”. Each character added a layer of love and life to the tale. Em’s courage, Finn’s “magical ability to make you smile even when things are grim”, Marina’s innocence, and James with all his GQ mad genius allure. I loved them all.<br /><br />And the time travel! Ms. Terrill explains, plays with, and depicts the wrinkles and science of time beautifully. Simply. You believe it can happen! The suspense and twists and turns had me leaning into the pages at some points. Just trying to get closer to the action. Closer to the characters. I will never forget Em, Finn, James and Marina. What they do for and to each other is heartbreaking and hopeful. A story that made me think and ask—How well do you know yourself? <br /><br />Highly recommended. Highly!<br /><br /><br />*Thomas—Thank you for the push to pick this one up. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11243671498296241297" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_958519316" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/958519316" />
    <a title="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction"><img alt="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605816027p2/2905339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/958519316?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" href="/user/show/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction">Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781452668963" href="/book/show/19301020-all-our-yesterdays">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer958519316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17861969784030538774">I’m going to keep this short and as sweet as I can because everyone seems to adore this story and sadly, I really didn’t. Before you beat me over the head with the fact that I am a moron who is too ignorant to follow a time-travel story, I have to say that I enjoyed both Stephen King’s 11/23/63 and The Time Traveler’s Wife so it wasn’t the time-travel bits that put me off. Those books worked for me because of the characters. Though this story has very strong characters and it was interesting to </span>
  <span id="freeText17861969784030538774" style="display:none">I’m going to keep this short and as sweet as I can because everyone seems to adore this story and sadly, I really didn’t. Before you beat me over the head with the fact that I am a moron who is too ignorant to follow a time-travel story, I have to say that I enjoyed both Stephen King’s 11/23/63 and The Time Traveler’s Wife so it wasn’t the time-travel bits that put me off. Those books worked for me because of the characters. Though this story has very strong characters and it was interesting to see how much Em changes as she matures, something about them just didn’t grab me enough to become emotionally invested in their story. I’m sure it’s a case of “it’s me, not you” and I’ll leave it at that.<br><br>Were I you and considering this audio I would recommend opting for the paperback instead. Something about the narrator’s tone, almost bordering on monotonous here and there, made it very difficult to get through and two of the characters, friends of Marina’s whose names escape me, were cringe inducing. One sounded like an insipid moron and the other sounded like some snooty old socialite with some sort of strange accent and I believe she was only 16 or so. The rest of the voices were decent but those two? Those two were truly awful. It's a good thing they only played bit parts or this would've been a DNF because the voices bothered me so much.<br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437058611ra/15532775.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>With that said, well, there's not much more to say. Everyone else loves it but I just thought it was okay.<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="17861969784030538774" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1949323812" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1949323812" />
    <a title="Inge" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6278820-inge"><img alt="Inge" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556214992p2/6278820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1949323812?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Inge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Inge" href="/user/show/6278820-inge">Inge</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18221260-all-our-yesterdays">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=pretty-fly-for-a-sci-fi">pretty-fly-for-a-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1949323812" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8048638120438478403">I really loved the premise of the book and the first 50% certainly delivered on the intrigue. The plot was thickening, the tension was building, and I was really curious to see how this was going to end! However, the second half ended up being really chaotic and repetitive. You blow up a balloon and release it and all the air flies out like pffrrrrtttt. That is my super professional description of what the book felt like to me.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rMD5VAZ7kwp0p0owq8lNQjj2MrKqcZns3qmUMPlUorEoT7KMcHjQmQBR6YiV/nC8NQDzryPCE5XN5g1qtVQO5A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mDrpCSJGbY+PAiW59M44ik34zguaxwmDGOAX9h7qdV8ctaLRVEUuHPv0hgHK+QV0QA4PFhN0g/oLr46sUurZCg==')})
  }
//]]>
